  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3e8844cf-46b8-460a-b62b-01bb9795321b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer12679089055564106046">One Fish Two Fish Red Fish Blue Fish is a 1960 children's book by Dr. Seuss (Theodor Seuss Geisel). A simple rhyming book for learner readers, it is a book with a freewheeling plot about a boy and a girl, and the many amazing creatures they have for friends and pets. One Fish Two Fish Red Fish Blue Fish was part of the Beginner Book Video series which included Oh, the Thin</span>
  <span id="freeText12679089055564106046" style="display:none">One Fish Two Fish Red Fish Blue Fish is a 1960 children's book by Dr. Seuss (Theodor Seuss Geisel). A simple rhyming book for learner readers, it is a book with a freewheeling plot about a boy and a girl, and the many amazing creatures they have for friends and pets. One Fish Two Fish Red Fish Blue Fish was part of the Beginner Book Video series which included Oh, the Thinks You Can Think! and The Foot Book.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2033945949" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7365405-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522094190p2/7365405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2033945949?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/7365405-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=2-fic-childrens">2-fic-childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=1-fiction">1-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2033945949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12364495160513525455"><b>
  <i>
    <u>Book Review</u>
  </i>
</b><br/>4 out of 5 stars for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7770.One_Fish__Two_Fish__Red_Fish__Blue_Fish' title='One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish by Dr. Seuss' rel='nofollow noopener'>One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish</a>, a children's picture book written in the 1960s by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/61105.Dr__Seuss' title='Dr. Seuss' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dr. Seuss</a>. I loved this one as a child, and probably read it around 7 or 8 years old, then again at 10. Between the rhymes and tongue-twisters, it encourages kids to laugh and have fun when reading. Focusing on pets, under water fish are my favorite. All the colors, shapes and sizes. All the things to do with them. Dr. Seuss is a definite children's classic, but </span>
  <span id="freeText12364495160513525455" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <u>Book Review</u>
  </i>
</b><br />4 out of 5 stars for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7770.One_Fish__Two_Fish__Red_Fish__Blue_Fish" title="One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish</a>, a children's picture book written in the 1960s by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/61105.Dr__Seuss" title="Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Dr. Seuss</a>. I loved this one as a child, and probably read it around 7 or 8 years old, then again at 10. Between the rhymes and tongue-twisters, it encourages kids to laugh and have fun when reading. Focusing on pets, under water fish are my favorite. All the colors, shapes and sizes. All the things to do with them. Dr. Seuss is a definite children's classic, but with pictures and movies being made, it helps bring it all full circle. I love buying these books for my friend's children, then sitting to read with them. Great memories!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>About Me</u>
  </i>
</b><br />For those new to me or my reviews... here's the scoop: I read A LOT. I write A LOT. And now I blog A LOT. First the book review goes on Goodreads, and then I send it on over to my WordPress blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thisismytruthnow.com">https://thisismytruthnow.com</a>, where you'll also find TV &amp; Film reviews, the revealing and introspective 365 Daily Challenge and lots of blogging about places I've visited all over the world. And you can find all my social media profiles to get the details on the who/what/when/where and my pictures. Leave a comment and let me know what you think. Vote in the poll and ratings. Thanks for stopping by.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12364495160513525455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_24186213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24186213" />
    <a title="Seth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63444-seth"><img alt="Seth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187495654p2/63444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24186213?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth" href="/user/show/63444-seth">Seth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63444-seth?shelf=lifelessons-poetry-childrens-etc">lifelessons-poetry-childrens-etc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24186213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7451976799067565568">(This review is in response to a request as to why I have only given <u>One Fish, Two Fish...</u> three stars)<br/><br/> Firmly ensconced in the middle tier of the Dr Seuss canon, <u>One Fish, Two Fish...</u> is many people's favorite for its light humor, catchy, Moliere-esque couplets, and clever use of repetition as well as surprise, as in the title, where the rhyming word comes at the beginning of a repeated syllable, rather than at the end of the phrase.<br/><br/> It earns its place as one of the most quotable (possibly only</span>
  <span id="freeText7451976799067565568" style="display:none">(This review is in response to a request as to why I have only given <u>One Fish, Two Fish...</u> three stars)<br /><br /> Firmly ensconced in the middle tier of the Dr Seuss canon, <u>One Fish, Two Fish...</u> is many people's favorite for its light humor, catchy, Moliere-esque couplets, and clever use of repetition as well as surprise, as in the title, where the rhyming word comes at the beginning of a repeated syllable, rather than at the end of the phrase.<br /><br /> It earns its place as one of the most quotable (possibly only <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23772.Green_Eggs_and_Ham" title="Green Eggs and Ham by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Green Eggs and Ham</a> is more often quoted) and fun to read aloud (after only <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/105551.Fox_in_Socks" title="Fox in Socks by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Fox in Socks</a>), but it stays firmly in the middle tier because it lacks three things: <br /><br /> 1) The classic Dr Seuss creations. That book doesn't introduce a Who, a Cat in the Hat, Mulberry Street, Green Eggs, Grinches, or other new element to our culture is not a criticism. It does, however, set those books apart as critical pieces that added to our society in some way; they rise above this book.<br /><br /> 2) Giesel's overt moralizing. Whether teaching is about size versus importance, making your own fun and cleaning up after it, the futility of war, or even a covert (and possibly unintentional) lesson on ambiguous modifiers, Seuss' classics do what the greatest children's literature does; they remind us as adults of lessons we needed to grow up and need now not to forget.<br /><br /> 3) Covert study of a philosophical principle. This may be all in interpretation (no one suggests that Giessel intended these), but many readers for decades have found the Seuss books' repetition and variation of a theme to serve as a metaphor or direct example of something universal. Whether it's a question of imagination in play and its social consequence (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233093.The_Cat_in_the_Hat" title="The Cat in the Hat by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cat in the Hat</a>), ontological questions about Platonic ideals (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23772.Green_Eggs_and_Ham" title="Green Eggs and Ham by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Green Eggs and Ham</a>, which rejects the notion that the environment is relevant to the enjoyment of the food), the Freudian question of experience and its ability to drive all future behavior (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113946.How_the_Grinch_Stole_Christmas_" title="How the Grinch Stole Christmas! by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">How the Grinch Stole Christmas</a>), or a more complex example such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28351.And_to_Think_That_I_Saw_it_on_Mulberry_Street" title="And to Think That I Saw it on Mulberry Street by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">To Think That I Saw it on Mulberry Street</a>, which combines all of the above in various ways), the very best of Seuss takes a universal question and circles it, showing us various views in fanciful ways while using childlike tropes to strip the question down to its abstract base. It doesn't do this because Giessel intended to be a philosopher, but because he though about children and learning in deep ways inherent to the essence of experiencing humanity. <br /><br /> In this context, <u>One Fish, Two Fish...</u> is a fine and enjoyable book, and one that I will enjoy reading many times; its three-star rating is only because it is a relative trifle in the Seuss canon when seen next to his many masterpieces. It isn't one you'll go back to over decades for inspiration, when teaching your children, or as an example to understand or explain a principle implicit to Giessel's thinking and vital to us all.<br /><br /> It's a great book. Get it. Read it. But it earns an "I Liked It" on the Goodreads scale. Don't think of passing up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/105551.Fox_in_Socks" title="Fox in Socks by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Fox in Socks</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7779.Horton_Hears_a_Who_" title="Horton Hears a Who! by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Horton Hears a Who</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233093.The_Cat_in_the_Hat" title="The Cat in the Hat by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cat in the Hat</a>, or other of his classics in favor of this one.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7451976799067565568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer285866895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10318703345202233456">Sheer poetry!<br/><br/><i>One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish</i> is a pure genius work of epic poetry. The beginning of the tale focuses on...you guessed it...fish. Pages and pages of fish with various characteristics (mostly harmless) are paraded before the reader in flashes of color and humor. But then (and this is where Dr. Seuss lost a star rating from me) the story veers off and begins introducing a random cast of beings more strange than an assortment of beasties rejected from a circus of the bizarre </span>
  <span id="freeText10318703345202233456" style="display:none">Sheer poetry!<br /><br /><i>One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish</i> is a pure genius work of epic poetry. The beginning of the tale focuses on...you guessed it...fish. Pages and pages of fish with various characteristics (mostly harmless) are paraded before the reader in flashes of color and humor. But then (and this is where Dr. Seuss lost a star rating from me) the story veers off and begins introducing a random cast of beings more strange than an assortment of beasties rejected from a circus of the bizarre for being too grotesque for the relatively polite society of carnies. Most appear to have been enslaved by a young boy and girl who claim these poor creatures are "pets," while forcing them into hard labor or using their mortal frames in mocked up games. Those who escape torture at the hands of the children are often no more fortunate. Take "Ned" for example. Ned does not fit in his bed, not his feet nor his head. It's absolutely tragic...</span>
  <a data-text-id="10318703345202233456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_19005385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19005385" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19005385?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=to-scoutie">to-scoutie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=to-my-kids">to-my-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=to-milos">to-milos</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=to-bronte">to-bronte</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=with-my-kids">with-my-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19005385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2919632132580215874">When I reach for a Dr. Seuss, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7770.One_Fish__Two_Fish__Red_Fish__Blue_Fish' title='One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish by Dr. Seuss' rel='nofollow noopener'>One Fish Two Fish Red Fish Blue Fish</a> is <u>never</u> the book I reach for. If I need something quick because the kids are late for bed, I grab <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/105549.The_Sneetches_and_Other_Stories' title='The Sneetches and Other Stories by Dr. Seuss' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sneetches</a> and pick a tale. If there's more time, but I'm still in a hurry, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23772.Green_Eggs_and_Ham__Beginner_Books_' title='Green Eggs and Ham (Beginner Books) by Dr. Seuss' rel='nofollow noopener'>Green Eggs and Ham</a> is the perfect choice. When two year old Scoutie wants a book, I grab the easiest Seuss of them all, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/206962.Hop_on_Pop' title='Hop on Pop by Dr. Seuss' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hop on Pop</a> (just as I did when the twins were babes). If I want to have some fun for myself, I grab the tongue twisterrific <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/105551.Fox_in_Socks' title='Fox in Socks by Dr. Seuss' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fox in Sock</a></span>
  <span id="freeText2919632132580215874" style="display:none">When I reach for a Dr. Seuss, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7770.One_Fish__Two_Fish__Red_Fish__Blue_Fish" title="One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">One Fish Two Fish Red Fish Blue Fish</a> is <u>never</u> the book I reach for. If I need something quick because the kids are late for bed, I grab <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/105549.The_Sneetches_and_Other_Stories" title="The Sneetches and Other Stories by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sneetches</a> and pick a tale. If there's more time, but I'm still in a hurry, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23772.Green_Eggs_and_Ham__Beginner_Books_" title="Green Eggs and Ham (Beginner Books) by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Green Eggs and Ham</a> is the perfect choice. When two year old Scoutie wants a book, I grab the easiest Seuss of them all, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/206962.Hop_on_Pop" title="Hop on Pop by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Hop on Pop</a> (just as I did when the twins were babes). If I want to have some fun for myself, I grab the tongue twisterrific <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/105551.Fox_in_Socks" title="Fox in Socks by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Fox in Socks</a>, and if it's closing in on Christmas, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113946.How_the_Grinch_Stole_Christmas_" title="How the Grinch Stole Christmas! by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">How the Grinch Stole Christmas</a> is the obvious choice. <br /><br />Hell, I am even more likely to read the Seuss-lite <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/460548.Go__Dog__Go_" title="Go, Dog. Go! by P.D. Eastman" rel="nofollow noopener">Go Dog. Go</a> than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7770.One_Fish__Two_Fish__Red_Fish__Blue_Fish" title="One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">One Fish Two Fish Red Fish Blue Fish</a>. But if my kids grab it, and Scoutie's been doing that a lot lately, I'll gladly traverse the bizaare landscape of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7770.One_Fish__Two_Fish__Red_Fish__Blue_Fish" title="One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish by Dr. Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">One Fish Two Fish Red Fish Blue Fish</a>. Of all Seuss's book, this is the least cohesive. It's just an excuse to rhyme. Nothing more than that. Mr. Brown makes an odd appearance. There's whiny Ned in his too small bed. Yet there's that great line: "From there to here, from here to there funny things are everywhere," and it's some of Seuss's best art. It's a good book. the kids love it, and Scoutie can't get enough. <br /><br />Honestly, I love it too. But I never reach for it and probably never will, which is okay ... it always winds up in my hands somehow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2919632132580215874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3108772026" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3108772026" />
    <a title="Daniel Clausen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/957634-daniel-clausen"><img alt="Daniel Clausen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603533755p2/957634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3108772026?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Clausen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Clausen" href="/user/show/957634-daniel-clausen">Daniel Clausen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957634-daniel-clausen?shelf=books-of-2019">books-of-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3108772026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4790289007409036919">One book, two book, red book, blue book...what a wonderful year it has been for reading! Instead of my normal book review, I thought I would use this last book review of the year to reflect on the year of reading. 2019 proved the old adage that the best investments are in old books and old friends. Since I consider books I've read before as old friends, it was a good year indeed! <br/><br/>The best of my re-reads included Murakami Haruki's Sputnik Sweetheart and Norwegian Wood. My own book "The Undergroun</span>
  <span id="freeText4790289007409036919" style="display:none">One book, two book, red book, blue book...what a wonderful year it has been for reading! Instead of my normal book review, I thought I would use this last book review of the year to reflect on the year of reading. 2019 proved the old adage that the best investments are in old books and old friends. Since I consider books I've read before as old friends, it was a good year indeed! <br /><br />The best of my re-reads included Murakami Haruki's Sputnik Sweetheart and Norwegian Wood. My own book "The Underground Novel", my satirical self-help novel, which I finished last year. Tales from the Irish Club by my old English teacher Lester Goran, the writing of Henry David Thoreau. I haven't decided what I will re-read next year, but shockingly that might include a biography of Elon Musk. <br /><br />That brings me to my biggest surprise of the year: a biography of Elon Musk. Though the writing was not a literary masterpiece, the subject matter was enthralling. So much so that I had to reflect on a simple question: Do I love biographies as a genre? It appears I do. One of my favorite books is a biography of Orson Welles. Thus, next year I'll do everything I can to lay my hands on more biographies. <br /><br />2019 was also a year of science. I read no less than three science books, my worst subject and enjoyed each of them. One of these books might find it onto my re-read list. One of the difficult things about reading science is that my critical blinkers are often turned off. I'm not sure how to engage these books in book reviews other than to note their value as entertainment, the accessibility, and their ability to motivate me to read other science books. Still, I'm not deterred. I will read at least one science book next year. <br /><br />2019 was also the year of "The Boys". I finally finished the comic book series I started when I was in graduate school. Why? I had to. I couldn't have the series ruined for me by things people were saying about the Amazon series. (I'm sure the Amazon series is fine, but I will always think of the series as something inspired by Bush-era silliness). <br /><br />The biggest disappointment this year: The big-think books. Nicholas Nassim Taleb is still a dazzling philosopher, but his newest book seems to see him indulge in his worst habits (picking petty fights with people who seem to annoy him on social media) rather than deepening and enriching his philosophy. At this point too, I seemed to have become able to anticipate what will be written in any given chapters (though to his credit he still has some surprises, read the section on -- How the Intolerant Minority wins!); 7 Habits of Successful People was a minor bust; The Subtle Art of Not Giving a Fuck and Essentialism were good books, but their usefulness for me was limited. I had already gotten their messages a long time ago. Alas, there was not a big "rethink" moment for me in 2019. <br /><br />Perhaps that means I'm just getting older and my reading is leading to a wiser life. Perhaps the big-think moments are actually in the genre of biography, not big think books. Actually, I'm pretty sure that's it. <br /><br />Having written all this, what is my take away for reading in 2020. Well, less but better. 30 books is fine for 2020 if they are the right ones. Spend more time vetting my books. Don't just pick up something because it seems convenient at the moment. It's hard to do, but it will pay off in the end. <br /><br />"I took the long way to choosing a book," I will write at the end of 2020, and I was all the better for it. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4790289007409036919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1808975" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1808975" />
    <a title="Sarah Sammis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/122647-sarah-sammis"><img alt="Sarah Sammis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181271036p2/122647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780394900131" href="/book/show/1610057.One_Fish_Two_Fish_Red_Fish_Blue_Fish">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=read-as-a-child">read-as-a-child</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=read-in-2002">read-in-2002</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1808975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13390230902795797244"> One of the joys of being a parent is sharing old favorites with my children. Harriet and Sean are now discovering Dr. Seuss. We are reading through all of his books and have landed on my all time favorite: One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish. From the time I was Harriet's age to being in second or third grade, I read this book on an almost daily basis. I really don't know how many times I've read it (either listening to it being read by one of my parents or reading it myself).<br/><br/>One Fish, Two </span>
  <span id="freeText13390230902795797244" style="display:none"> One of the joys of being a parent is sharing old favorites with my children. Harriet and Sean are now discovering Dr. Seuss. We are reading through all of his books and have landed on my all time favorite: One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish. From the time I was Harriet's age to being in second or third grade, I read this book on an almost daily basis. I really don't know how many times I've read it (either listening to it being read by one of my parents or reading it myself).<br /><br />One Fish, Two Fish... begins with this little dedication: "From there to here, from here to there, funny things are everywhere." This book revels in the silly. It starts off simply enough with fish of different color and fish of different ages. Then it spirals out of control with fish driving cars and even sillier things.<br /><br />The book doesn't have a plot. It's a series of tongue twisters presented as short scenes, almost like vaudeville routines. Witnessing these different examples of silly are a boy and a girl (or a Sean and a Harriet as my children see things). They watch creatures run (just for fun), different animals with different feet (and numbers of legs), and they go on a ride with Mr. Gump's Wump. There is Ned and his bed with holes in the most annoying of places. I wonder if he'll ever get a descent night's sleep? There are animals for opening cans, and others for boxing, ones who have hair for brushing and so forth.<br /><br />In all of this silliness are Dr. Seuss's illustrations. All of the creatures have Seuss's unique style, being somewhat shaggy (even the fish). I can remember sometimes just flipping through the book to enjoy the drawings. My favorites are the pink ink drinking yink, can opening zans, the sleep walking sheep and the hook cook book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13390230902795797244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1542554426" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10827825-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571182054p2/10827825.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1542554426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9854103102808239602">The rhyming and tongue twisters are a great way to introduce young readers to the way that words can be used. The illustrations of weird and wonderful creatures are whimsical and a great way for children to use their imagination. Being presented with creatures that are not real can sometimes be a challenge for younger readers, but I believe that this can a great way to start conversations with children about the characters. Finding out what they think these creatures might be, what they do, how </span>
  <span id="freeText9854103102808239602" style="display:none">The rhyming and tongue twisters are a great way to introduce young readers to the way that words can be used. The illustrations of weird and wonderful creatures are whimsical and a great way for children to use their imagination. Being presented with creatures that are not real can sometimes be a challenge for younger readers, but I believe that this can a great way to start conversations with children about the characters. Finding out what they think these creatures might be, what they do, how they make them feel. <br /><br />All in all a fantastic book for readers both young and old. </span>

<div id="review_2985201721" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2985201721" />
    <a title="Rosemary Standeven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36933045-rosemary-standeven"><img alt="Rosemary Standeven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451831847p2/36933045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2985201721?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosemary Standeven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosemary Standeven" href="/user/show/36933045-rosemary-standeven">Rosemary Standeven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007425617" href="/book/show/13649974-one-fish-two-fish-red-fish-blue-fish-dr-seuss">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2985201721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14166957811104415587">On Monday, on the BBC TV quiz ‘Only Connect’ there was a question where you had to guess the 4th in the sequence:<br/><br/>	[Michael Fish picture] [Michael Fish, Michael Fish] ? 	?<br/><br/>Once my husband had identified Michael Fish (ex-TV metereologist), I knew the answer was “One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish”, without having the faintest idea why. It just sounded right. The answer was then given, stating that it was a Dr.Seuss book.<br/>Then on Tuesday, at the pub quiz, we had to decipher three book titles:<br/>1 F</span>
  <span id="freeText14166957811104415587" style="display:none">On Monday, on the BBC TV quiz ‘Only Connect’ there was a question where you had to guess the 4th in the sequence:<br /><br />	[Michael Fish picture] [Michael Fish, Michael Fish] ? 	?<br /><br />Once my husband had identified Michael Fish (ex-TV metereologist), I knew the answer was “One Fish, Two Fish, Red Fish, Blue Fish”, without having the faintest idea why. It just sounded right. The answer was then given, stating that it was a Dr.Seuss book.<br />Then on Tuesday, at the pub quiz, we had to decipher three book titles:<br />1 F, 2 F, R F, B F		(also S 5, and A T o 2 C)<br />There was that book again! I could not recall having read it, and my husband had never heard of it, so there was only one thing left to do. On Wednesday, I ordered a copy. It arrived on Friday, and now on Saturday I have read it and am writing my review.<br />I love it!<br />The illustrations are superbly fabulous, and the rhyming text anarchically silly. This is not a book to teach children about reality (it does have ‘lessons’ on counting and colours) – it is a book about the way words sound, and all the fun you can have with rhyming. Incidentally, it will help children learn to read, as they see how similar sounding words look similar too. But, for me, the pleasure of reading it, was in the way it sounded and looked. <br /><br />e.g. “If you like to go Bump! Bump! <br /> just jump on the hump of the Wump of Gump”<br /><br /> “if you wish to wish a wish, <br /> you may swish for fish <br /> with my Ish wish dish”<br /><br />This is a great book for any child – whether they are reading for reading yet or not. It is also fun for middle-aged non-parents!<br />I will be passing this lovely book on to two of our pub quiz team mates who have a one-year-old child. It is never too early to start kids on books.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14166957811104415587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2nvqLQYtG8kz6SLz4p//TtlnCV9MXY+UJeBHZMsGGKUPO1mNrcKxM/7PmnUMMygojKtUS3X2GQkKr9E/aIYK+Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Kg/YlHDh6k8rpIZlk4dR4UPe6LmtYmaWWESnD76HPov/T2s02w5AteaCPuN9K4aHFhK1rZTJ8At3CzFUHQcs1w==')})
  }

Using the pseudonym of &quot;Dr. Seuss&quot; (Seuss was Geisel\'s middle name) and only two hundred twenty-three words, Geisel created a replacement for those dull primers: &quot;The Cat in the Hat.&quot; The instant success of the book prompted Geisel and his wife to found Beginner Books, and Geisel wrote many popular books in this series, including &quot;Hop on Pop,&quot; &quot;Fox in Socks,&quot; and &quot;Green Eggs and Ham.&quot; \n\nOther favorite titles in this series are &quot;Go, Dog, Go!&quot; and &quot;Are You My Mother?&quot; by P. D. Eastman, &quot;A Fly Went By,&quot; by Mike McClintock, and &quot;Put Me in the Zoo,&quot; by Robert Lopshire. These affordable hardcover books combine large print, easy vocabulary, and large, bright illustrations in stories kids will want to read again and again.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/61105.Dr_Seuss">About Dr. Seuss</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/61105.Dr_Seuss"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1193930952p3/61105.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/61105.Dr_Seuss">Dr. Seuss
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
16,563
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15749062479632745020">Theodor Seuss Geisel was born 2 March 1904 in Springfield, MA. He graduated Dartmouth College in 1925, and proceeded on to Oxford University with the intent of acquiring a doctorate in literature. At Oxford he met Helen Palmer, who he wed in 1927. He returned from Europe in 1927, and began working for a magazine called Judge, the leading humor magazine in America at the time, submitting both carto</span>
  <span id="freeText15749062479632745020" style="display:none">Theodor Seuss Geisel was born 2 March 1904 in Springfield, MA. He graduated Dartmouth College in 1925, and proceeded on to Oxford University with the intent of acquiring a doctorate in literature. At Oxford he met Helen Palmer, who he wed in 1927. He returned from Europe in 1927, and began working for a magazine called Judge, the leading humor magazine in America at the time, submitting both cartoons and humorous articles for them. Additionally, he was submitting cartoons to Life, Vanity Fair and Liberty. In some of his works, he'd made reference to an insecticide called Flit. These references gained notice, and led to a contract to draw comic ads for Flit. This association lasted 17 years, gained him national exposure, and coined the catchphrase "Quick, Henry, the Flit!" <br /><br />In 1936 on the way to a vaction in Europe, listening to the rhythm of the ship's engines, he came up with And to Think That I Saw It on Mulberry Street, which was then promptly rejected by the first 43 publishers he showed it to. Eventually in 1937 a friend published the book for him, and it went on to at least moderate success. <br /><br />During WW II, Geisel joined the army and was sent to Hollywood. Captain Geisel would write for Frank Capra's Signal Corps Unit (for which he won the Legion of Merit) and do documentaries (he won Oscar's for Hitler Lives and Design for Death). He also created a cartoon called Gerald McBoing-Boing which also won him an Oscar. <br /><br />In May of 1954, Life published a report concerning illiteracy among school children. The report said, among other things, that children were having trouble to read because their books were boring. This inspired Geisel's publisher, and prompted him to send Geisel a list of 400 words he felt were important, asked him to cut the list to 250 words (the publishers idea of how many words at one time a first grader could absorb), and write a book. Nine months later, Geisel, using 220 of the words given to him published The Cat in the Hat, which went on to instant success. <br /><br />In 1960 Bennett Cerf bet Geisel $50 that he couldn't write an entire book using only fifty words. The result was Green Eggs and Ham. Cerf never paid the $50 from the bet. <br /><br />Helen Palmer Geisel died in 1967. Theodor Geisel married Audrey Stone Diamond in 1968. Theodor Seuss Geisel died 24 September 1991. <br /><br />Also worked under the pen name:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/398177.Theo_Le_Sieg" rel="nofollow noopener">Theo Le Sieg</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15749062479632745020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
